Bud and Papa Roja then manage to convince us to stay in town another evening. 100 (Sat 7/24); Lander, Wyoming\n\nThis morning after we packed up and were in the process of heading to breakfast, we learned from someone we were passing that there was a farmers market in the park. So we decided to stay there and get breakfast from the local vendors, and we also learned that an art festival was happening concurrently in the park. We hung out for the beginning of the art fair and watched the local fire department child drum and bagpipe corp perform. We then left to get more caffeine, meet up with Nude Beach who stayed in a hotel, check out the gear store, and hangout out the library to charge up our batteries. The librarians remembered us from yesterday and our glowing review of the library. They took our pictures and asked us to write something because apparently the library is regularly on the chopping block when it comes to city budget. Bison asks to play the piano in the little theatre room we saw, and they ended up taking us to the original library building, which was a Carnegie Library (look it up) that has a baby grand piano. We play piano, sing, charge, and download for a few hours before we head out for a late lunch. We then went back to the pool for another soak before resupplying, where we run into Nibbles and Threshold! We pick up Dominos pizza, head back to the park to celebrate Christmas in July by watching Christmas television episodes, then sleep in the dugout again. Adventure Responsibly, we are all about encouraging enjoying our public lands in a responsible way! Here's 5 easy tips to have a responsible visit to Arches National Park:\n\n-Timed Entry reservation is required \nFrom April 3 to October 3, 2022 Arches will implement a temporary, pilot timed entry system to help manage traffic and improve visitor experiences.Visit nps.gov/arch for more info\n\n-No drones allowed (as in any national park)\nIt is always unlawful to launch, fly and land a drone inside National Parks\n\n-Watch your step for delicate cryptobiotic soil\nArches is home to a unique living soil crust. ‚ÄúOnce damaged, crusts may take many years to grow back. Areas that have been stripped of crusts are vulnerable to erosion, flooding, dust storms, loss of organic materials, and invasion by non-native weeds that thrive on disturbed soil.‚Äù-NPS\n\n-‚ÄùLight Painting‚Äù photography is prohibited in the park.\n‚ÄúNote that using artificial light sources to light up landscapes, rock formations, or other park features is prohibited. - NPS\n\n-Always stay hydrated and be prepared for varying temps.\nHydration is a key factor for any adventure. Arches is a high-desert environment with wildly shifting temperatures. Basically what it feels like is that air is getting stuck in my throat and when I try to take a deep breath, it can't get through. I have to try a few times before one breath finally makes it through. I can also feel like I have a tight throat, like a heaviness in my throat. This is a rare condition and it could be connected to my focal dystonia I've had since I was young. I'm on month 7 of a 8 month waitlist to see a neurologist. \n\nIt gets worse when I exercise, poor air quality, strong smells, etc... but when I lay down I can feel better. \n\nI have covid again but it doesn't seem to affect this issue. I had a bad sore throat yesterday and my breathing issue was surprisingly okay. \n\nThis started in 2013. And has been around since but I was doing a lot better until 3 months ago. I feel crippled. I can't really exercise and I've been gaining weight. Of course its been affecting my mental health because I love being active and I can't do that anymore. \n\nI've been reading a lot, and navigating our flawed healthcare system in hope someone can help me and the good news is, I have made some progress in finding someone. \n\nI miss being able to run, or hike. I get on IG and see everyone going outside and it has made me very envious. We really don't realize how much we take for granted. I feel like my body and soul have been torn apart and I have to rebuild myself to get back to where I was two years ago. \n\nAnyway. Thanks for reading. \n\nPhoto from July 99 (Fri 7/23) 3 Trail Miles \u0026 A Hitch into Lander\n\nWe woke up this morning and packed up immediately without breakfast because we only had about an hour of hiking before we'd get to the road. We throw out the thumb and get picked up by an RV covered in cartoon characters and with three cats inside. It's piloted by a nice retired couple who let their grandchildren paint the outside. They drop us off at the post office, we grab our packages with our bear gear (we're heading into grizzly territory!), and then get McDonald's. We then go into tow and, hit up the library to upload podcast recordings. We check out the church where there is supposedly going to be a community potluck later, go eat some very tasty ice cream, and then head to the local high school where the pool is open for public use. This week‚Äôs episode in @bigbendnps is no exception. Why do some among us behave so irresponsibly?\n‚Üü\nOne theory I‚Äôm willing to test states that our rash of recent infractions are simply due to the percentages. Since COVID forced so many indoors for so long, a higher number of people than before recreate outdoors upon emergence from lock-down. These large numbers also translate into a higher number (but equal %) of yo-yos spending time in campgrounds, national parks, and on hiking trails. More people, more dupewads. Thankfully, I actually noticed far fewer people on our local trails in 2021 than in 2020, so if this percentage play really does correlate with these increases in irresponsible behavior, then I‚Äôm satisfied that as this crazy world eventually returns to ‚Äúnormal,‚Äù the crowds and number of bozos will eventually diminish.\n‚Üü\nAnother theory I have is that ubiquitous cameras and closed-network sharing are to blame.
